<div id="review_2863808882" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2863808882" />
    <a title="Wally Flangers" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/75111402-wally-flangers"><img alt="Wally Flangers" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1513621589p2/75111402.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2863808882?book_show_action=true">Jul 24, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wally Flangers" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wally Flangers" href="/user/show/75111402-wally-flangers">Wally Flangers</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/32884757-black-house">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2863808882" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13546535995958496538">It’s very rare for me to give a book a 5 star rating, but like “The Talisman”, I absolutely loved “Black House”…. This was, however, completely shocking for me because I absolutely hated the first 40 to 60 pages and was wondering how I was going to make it through 625 pages if it kept on going the way it was. The opening chapter, especially, had WAY TOO MANY character introductions and details of the town with unnecessary back stories of every store in the area for my brain to process. But once </span>
  <span id="freeText13546535995958496538" style="display:none">It’s very rare for me to give a book a 5 star rating, but like “The Talisman”, I absolutely loved “Black House”…. This was, however, completely shocking for me because I absolutely hated the first 40 to 60 pages and was wondering how I was going to make it through 625 pages if it kept on going the way it was. The opening chapter, especially, had WAY TOO MANY character introductions and details of the town with unnecessary back stories of every store in the area for my brain to process. But once I painfully grinded though that endless introduction, everything immediately clicked.<br /><br />You may be wondering how a book that I rated so high took me a month to read but it only took an excessive amount of time because I had a lot going on this month, including a family vacation with kids…. In addition, I was also reading “Skeleton Crew” at the same time, which isn’t exactly a short book.... But trust me, I was addicted to Black House and couldn’t wait until the next reading session to continue the story.<br /><br />Black House is the sequel to “The Talisman” and is probably the most connected tie-in to the Dark Tower series, so it is highly recommended that you read it if you are reading the Dark Tower…. The story is narrated in third-person omniscient and is about a serial killer nicknamed, “The Fisherman”, who is responsible for murdering children in the town of French Landing, Wisonsin after consuming their remains. One particular boy named, Tyler Marshall, is the latest to be abducted and is sought after by Jack Sawyer (the main character in “The Talisman”), the French Landing Police Department, and a gang of pissed off locals…. Tyler is kept alive by The Fisherman, who serves the Crimson King (the main antagonistic being from the Dark Tower series), with a mission of bringing him to Black House to serve as a “Breaker”. Tyler happens to be one of the most powerful Breakers there has ever been and the Crimson King needs the boy’s powers to break the remaining beams that hold up the Dark Tower and end all worlds.<br /><br />My favorite part about Black House was the increasing pace and build-up of suspense. I enjoy stories where some foreshadowing occurs and little details that seem irrelevant end up coming together later in the book. I also liked seeing Jack Sawyer as an adult and the reminiscence of the events that occurred when he was a boy (which took place in “The Talisman”).<br /><br />Although the ending was somewhat abrupt, as the final battle inside Black House wasn’t as epic as it could have been, it recovered extremely well with a little twist a the end and a short Epilogue to wrap the story up. The Epilogue also leaves the story open for a third book, although I think the chances of a third one ever being published are very slim.<br /><br />I will offer you a great piece of advice if you have not read Black House yet…. Although this is considered somewhat of a stand-alone novel by many readers, it really isn’t in a lot of ways. If you haven’t read “The Talisman”, then you will be lost once you come across some of the references and back stories in “Black House”. It is also important that you get some back story on Jack Sawyer, Speedy Parker, and how “the Territories” work…. It will definitely help you understand what’s going on and you will be happy you did. Plus, “The Talisman” is an awesome read anyway, so you can’t lose.<br /><br />FINAL VERDICT: I give this book 5 out of 5 stars. I can’t say enough good things about Black House and really like how Stephen King and Peter Straub’s writing styles come together. The book is a perfect blend of drama, horror, and mystery and I would recommend it to any fan of those genres.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13546535995958496538" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_44683868" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/44683868" />
    <a title="Chris " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1956959-chris"><img alt="Chris " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1502408626p2/1956959.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/44683868?book_show_action=true">Jan 28, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chris " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chris " href="/user/show/1956959-chris">Chris </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/539127.Black_House">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1956959-chris?shelf=read-owned-hardcover">read-owned-hardcover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1956959-chris?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer44683868" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13236958796460492829">I absolutely loved this book. It's funny, because I picked it up immediately after reading <i>The Talisman</i>, and at first I was put off by the shift in tone and feel of this one. I wanted more Talisman style fantasy adventure, with the lovable young Jack Sawyer. What I got was a cold, detached, present-tense narrative that watched everything from above and showed a landscape that was totally out of place with the book I had just finished. This is supposed to be a sequel!<br/><br/>But am I ever glad I stuck wi</span>
  <span id="freeText13236958796460492829" style="display:none">I absolutely loved this book. It's funny, because I picked it up immediately after reading <i>The Talisman</i>, and at first I was put off by the shift in tone and feel of this one. I wanted more Talisman style fantasy adventure, with the lovable young Jack Sawyer. What I got was a cold, detached, present-tense narrative that watched everything from above and showed a landscape that was totally out of place with the book I had just finished. This is supposed to be a sequel!<br /><br />But am I ever glad I stuck with it. The present voice grew to become a comfort, and as the narrator became more attached to the characters, so did I. This is still not the same book, but oh my, what a book it is.<br /><br />I said that <i>The Talisman</i> reminded me somewhat of a blend of <i>Lord of the Rings</i> and <i>Tom Sawyer</i>. Well, for this one, throw in some <i>Silence of the Lambs</i> and even a touch of <i>The Good, the Bad, and the Ugly.</i> The villains were delightful in how wicked-evil they could be. The heroes were flawed, yes, but so human and I couldn't help but pull for them all the way. There were even a few times near the end where I wanted to pitch the book out the window. But I couldn't, as I had to keep reading until there was no more.<br /><br />I've heard that King and Straub are planning a third collaboration. After reading <i>Black House</i> I must say I hope they do. And I won't wait 9 years to read the next one, I can say that much.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13236958796460492829" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15939840598760883646">This was one of the first King books I read as a teen and I read it not knowing it was the sequel to The Talisman. Now that I’ve read The Talisman and reread Black House, it’s like all the puzzle pieces finally fit together. I loved Black House but reading it again with all the missing pieces filled in made me love it all that much more. There’s something about this story that just gets under my skin and really creeps me the fuck out!</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_293635452" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/293635452" />
    <a title="Lauryn April" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8179769-lauryn-april"><img alt="Lauryn April" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1480905053p2/8179769.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/293635452?book_show_action=true">Mar 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lauryn April" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lauryn April" href="/user/show/8179769-lauryn-april">Lauryn April</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer293635452" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12006298059964758731">I've read a number of Stephen King's books, enough to consider him one of my favorite authors; and out of everything I've read by him I enjoyed this, along with The Talisman, the most. This has encouraged me to start looking at some of Peter Straub's work as well; however I have yet to do so at this time. What this book has done is inspire me to get into his Dark Tower series, which I had been avoiding doing for some time because I'd heard that it was slow getting into. If that series has ever i</span>
  <span id="freeText12006298059964758731" style="display:none">I've read a number of Stephen King's books, enough to consider him one of my favorite authors; and out of everything I've read by him I enjoyed this, along with The Talisman, the most. This has encouraged me to start looking at some of Peter Straub's work as well; however I have yet to do so at this time. What this book has done is inspire me to get into his Dark Tower series, which I had been avoiding doing for some time because I'd heard that it was slow getting into. If that series has ever interested you I would suggest reading The Talisman and Black House as they will certainly be the tipping point to get you into that series.<br /><br />The world that King and Straub create in this book is a place that I think as kids we all envision exists, it's a fantasy world, but they make it real. You see much more of it in The Talisman, but I find that fitting because in Black House, the main character, Jack is no longer a thirteen year old boy; he's a grown man and he needs to rediscover this world outside our own. Something that I think is much harder for adults to do. This is a very different story then The Talisman, but it is so for a reason and I enjoyed seeing this little boy that I followed on his quest across country all grown up. His adventures as an adult should be different.<br /><br />Since reading this I've found references to this 'other world' in many of King's other books such as Lisley's Story, which I also greatly enjoyed, and smaller references in a number of other books. Every time I read one and I see that little reference it sucks me in and I want to know more about this place which the Talisman and Black House name the Territories.<br /><br />As usual with King, this book had its moments that literally sent chills down my spine. It didn't scare me to the point where I was afraid to sleep at night like Salem's Lot did when I was twelve, or even Bag of Bones, when I was twenty three. But, it did have one of the most disturbing villains I think King has ever created.<br /><br />This book was also my inspiration to dabble in the present tense with my writing. I find King and Straub tackle this tense perfectly and use it to build suspense. What you're reading is happening now and that makes it all feel so much more intense. Present tense can throw people off sometimes, but for this book I would throw away all preconceived notions that Novels should only be written in the past tense.<br /><br />For More Reviews by Lauryn April, go to <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://laurynapril.blogspot.com">http://laurynapril.blogspot.com</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="12006298059964758731" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Abbie | ab_reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Abbie | ab_reads" href="/user/show/53055819-abbie-ab-reads">Abbie | ab_reads</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1950905531" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10880127783635753499">3.5 stars<br/><br/>Unlike The Talisman, this collaboration between my beloved King and Peter Straub fell a little flat for me. I'm quite upset, this is my first less than 4 star King!<br/><br/>I am not going to list all the things I didn't like about this book because I don't particularly like putting negative reviews out there, as I don't want people to not read the book and form their own opinions!! I will just say, for the negative parts, I did not like the narrative style, I didn't connect with Jack as much as </span>
  <span id="freeText10880127783635753499" style="display:none">3.5 stars<br /><br />Unlike The Talisman, this collaboration between my beloved King and Peter Straub fell a little flat for me. I'm quite upset, this is my first less than 4 star King!<br /><br />I am not going to list all the things I didn't like about this book because I don't particularly like putting negative reviews out there, as I don't want people to not read the book and form their own opinions!! I will just say, for the negative parts, I did not like the narrative style, I didn't connect with Jack as much as in the Talisman, the first 350 pages were such a drag for me that even the great final 200ish pages couldn't pull it up to a 4 star rating. SORRY Black House fans!<br /><br />HOWEVER I did enjoy some aspects! We were introduced to some great new characters such as the Thunder Five, I especially liked Doc and Beezer, and Henry Leydon. Some of the scenes with Henry (you'll know which ones I'm talking about) truly gave me chills! And of course, all those Dark Tower tie-ins! Beams! Breakers! Roland! I lived for it honestly, so well done! Which makes me wonder if I'd have enjoyed it more if it were written solely by King...ah well!<br /></span>

<div id="review_646499896" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/646499896" />
    <a title="Kathryn" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6504379-kathryn"><img alt="Kathryn" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590065910p2/6504379.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/646499896?book_show_action=true">Jun 20, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathryn" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathryn" href="/user/show/6504379-kathryn">Kathryn</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780345441034" href="/book/show/18129.Black_House">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6504379-kathryn?shelf=horror-read">horror-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6504379-kathryn?shelf=buddy-reads">buddy-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6504379-kathryn?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6504379-kathryn?shelf=stephen-king-read">stephen-king-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6504379-kathryn?shelf=did-not-finish">did-not-finish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer646499896" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10684528005390912980">I don't even know what to say about this book, except for negative things. Not only did I not finish this book, but I am left completely disappointed in it. I was expecting the same fuel The Talisman had for me, which I really, really enjoyed. Boy, was I disappointed. Not only was the storyline disappointing, the writing for me, was a disaster in the slow as molasses department. <br/><br/>I was excited about reading this with the friends I read it with, but now, I am left with really nothing nice to say a</span>
  <span id="freeText10684528005390912980" style="display:none">I don't even know what to say about this book, except for negative things. Not only did I not finish this book, but I am left completely disappointed in it. I was expecting the same fuel The Talisman had for me, which I really, really enjoyed. Boy, was I disappointed. Not only was the storyline disappointing, the writing for me, was a disaster in the slow as molasses department. <br /><br />I was excited about reading this with the friends I read it with, but now, I am left with really nothing nice to say about it. There were times the story would get mildly interesting, but for the most part, nothing held my attention, and even the slightly more interesting parts were boring. <br /><br />After reading over 250 pages, I put the book down in the hopes a break from it would help me to get back on track and give me some momentum to finish it. I found myself putting it back on my bookshelf and not even caring to know what happens. If there is a third installment, I really hope it is of the same quality as The Talisman instead of this mess. I guess I am just disappointed this came from King.</span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2752554668" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2752554668" />
    <a title="Lena Puro" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/57251668-lena-puro"><img alt="Lena Puro" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1467256499p2/57251668.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2752554668" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14027936877844950476">This is actually a sequel to "The Talisman" written with Peter Straub. Quite long like most of King's books, but I always enjoy the ride. Following Jack Sawyer's investigative talents (who kind of doesn't really want to get involved) we find ourselves in a small town where children are disappearing, apparently being eaten. Jack befriends the town cop, some bikers, and begins to unravel the "other" world that seems to blend with "French Landing" with its token crazies, crows, and lurid old men. J</span>
  <span id="freeText14027936877844950476" style="display:none">This is actually a sequel to "The Talisman" written with Peter Straub. Quite long like most of King's books, but I always enjoy the ride. Following Jack Sawyer's investigative talents (who kind of doesn't really want to get involved) we find ourselves in a small town where children are disappearing, apparently being eaten. Jack befriends the town cop, some bikers, and begins to unravel the "other" world that seems to blend with "French Landing" with its token crazies, crows, and lurid old men. Jack is asked to consult on the investigation of the most current missing young boy - Tyler Marshall (whose mom has gone "Bye-Bye") and the plot unfolds. Still wish he could write without swearing, but that's the world we live in! (Actually he CAN as demonstrated by his book written for his daughter "Eyes of the Dragon.") </span>

The Tower , The Beam! <br>Jack meets, the mother of the murdered boy, Judy.               <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/22765690-terry?shelf=horror">horror</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2003949019" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1431065738351208998">I actually enjoyed this a little more than The Talisman. However, I would say that if you did not like The Talisman, you may not enjoy this one either. It does have a darker, more horror-like feel to it. Overall, I enjoyed it. Liked getting back to see Jack Sawyer. I'm Looking forward to the third book, if it is ever written, although I probably would want to read the Dark Tower series before I read it. Overall, I would say 3.5/5 stars rounded up.</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer18442059317134947486">Stephen King and Peter Straub apparently decided that, since their last collaboration was so <b>great</b>, they would try to follow it with an astounding book that broke every single writing rule in existence. I believe the effort is a prime example of why those rules were made in the first place. Amen.</span>

          </span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2653833805" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2653833805" />
    <a title="Jason" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4014393-jason"><img alt="Jason" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1578190142p2/4014393.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2653833805?book_show_action=true">Apr 29, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jason" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jason" href="/user/show/4014393-jason">Jason</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover " href="/book/show/539127.Black_House">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">horror/fantasy/thriller</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Jason by: </span>
      SK Bibliography
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4014393-jason?shelf=favorite-heroes-protagonists">favorite-heroes-protagonists</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4014393-jason?shelf=stephen-king">stephen-king</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4014393-jason?shelf=dead-or-injured-dog-warning">dead-or-injured-dog-warning</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4014393-jason?shelf=best-of-the-year">best-of-the-year</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4014393-jason?shelf=2019">2019</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2653833805" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12931932210719262871"><b>Favorite new book read in 2019</b><br/><br/><a href='https://imgur.com/kQpJJoG' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1556679396i/27437797.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Finally, the Rock has finished all of Stephen King's novels... Well, I don't know if the Rock has or not, but <i>I have</i>! I intentionally left this one for last because I thought it would suck. I thought it would suck because <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/116530056' title='Sorry, I gotta call it like I see it.' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Talisman</a> sucked and this is the sequel. Boy, was I wrong. It's a shame I gave this so much unwarranted contempt prior to investigation, but it's also nice to go out on a five star read. Well done Messrs. King and Straub.<br/><br/>Allow me another par</span>
  <span id="freeText12931932210719262871" style="display:none"><b>Favorite new book read in 2019</b><br><br><a href="https://imgur.com/kQpJJoG" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1556679396i/27437797.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Finally, the Rock has finished all of Stephen King's novels... Well, I don't know if the Rock has or not, but <i>I have</i>! I intentionally left this one for last because I thought it would suck. I thought it would suck because <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/116530056" title="Sorry, I gotta call it like I see it." rel="nofollow noopener">The Talisman</a> sucked and this is the sequel. Boy, was I wrong. It's a shame I gave this so much unwarranted contempt prior to investigation, but it's also nice to go out on a five star read. Well done Messrs. King and Straub.<br><br>Allow me another paragraph before I get to the review. I started this Stephen King journey 15 years ago with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/116529769" title="my review" rel="nofollow noopener">It</a>. Little did I know that I was leading off with what would be not only my favorite SK book, but one of my favorite books of all time. <i>It</i> vies for second place with <i>Peter Pan</i> from time to time (and is currently the winner in that contest), but I'm afraid it never really knocks <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/118640145" title="my review of the undisputed winner" rel="nofollow noopener">A Christmas Carol</a> out of the top spot. But within King's bibliography, I put <i>It</i> on a pedestal, and all others fight for second place. <i>Black House</i> will probably never get there (the competition is pretty stiff with <i>The Dark Tower</i> series, <i>Duma Key</i>, and <i>Needful Things</i> after all), but it's on the top tier.<br><br>Just like every writer, King has his own style, though it's evolved over his 40+ year career. Sometimes his stuff works, sometimes it doesn't. With this he's firing on all cylinders. Maybe it was pairing up with Straub that helped it along; I don't know. But it's just right, like baby bear's porridge. The townspeople are believably crazy. (It seems like all of SK's towns are able to screw things up worse than Mayberry, NC.) The background info on the side characters isn't excessive, but gives them a little depth. The secondary antagonists, especially Wendell Green, are infuriating, but get the right amount of comeuppance along the way while also catching a break from time to time. The <i>Dark Tower</i> tie-ins fit just right. The many references to other works that have nothing to do with this story (e.g. <a href="https://stephenking.fandom.com/wiki/Rose_Red" title="SK Wiki page" rel="nofollow noopener">Rose Red</a> which I'm afraid is a guilty pleasure) are just mentioned for the fan boys and then left alone; there's no extra line or two obnoxiously jerking you out of the story which is a major failing in some of King's other works such as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2141935192" title="my review" rel="nofollow noopener">Sleeping Beauties</a>. In short, whoever edited this should be allowed to give some of King's later books the same treatment. Or maybe it was Straub encouraging him to can that shit in which case they should collaborate more often... Wait, I better think carefully about that because as far as I'm concerned their first collaboration left a lot to be desired.<br><br>Anyway, what's great about this? I liked our tour guide narrator. At first I thought it was annoying, but I got on board pretty quickly and enjoyed the ride. The side protagonist Henry was cool as a fan. As for our main character, Jack... He was fine in <i>The Talisman</i>, but he's so awesome in this I want to marry him or something. The villains set against him matched up just right, and while they weren't anything to write home about when compared to other King baddies (which is saying something for those others because the Fisherman, a cannibalistic, serial child murderer, was pretty damn heinous), he and Mr. Munshun were equal to Jack. Roland would've wasted both of them without batting an eye, but Jack ain't Roland. Hell, who is?<br><br>One amusing thing in here is all the praise for Mark McGwire. (Baseball is one of the minor themes woven throughout, if you can believe that...) This was written mostly in 2000 and early 2001. I wonder if King and Straub still feel the same way about him.<br><br>If you like Stephen King, and want more depth from the Dark Tower series, then read this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12931932210719262871" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_3508486399" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3508486399" />
    <a title="latham" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/68089240-latham"><img alt="latham" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1582607939p2/68089240.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3508486399?book_show_action=true">Oct 23, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="latham" class="user" itemprop="url" name="latham" href="/user/show/68089240-latham">latham</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Mass Market Paperback 9780007100446" href="/book/show/65512.Black_House">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68089240-latham?shelf=stephen-king-ranked">stephen-king-ranked</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/68089240-latham?shelf=scaryyy-books">scaryyy-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3508486399" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7773780295556259473">the sheer vastness of black house makes it a little difficult to talk about. a combination of the talisman and the dark tower, alongside a detective murder/mystery inside the small town of french landing; black house has a lot going on and was at risk of becoming a convoluted, confusing mess. <br/><br/>good thing it isn't. black house is spooky!. the atmosphere in this thing is just so creepy. if i never go to french landing, i will live a happy man haha. i loved the exploration of this town's people, the</span>
  <span id="freeText7773780295556259473" style="display:none">the sheer vastness of black house makes it a little difficult to talk about. a combination of the talisman and the dark tower, alongside a detective murder/mystery inside the small town of french landing; black house has a lot going on and was at risk of becoming a convoluted, confusing mess. <br /><br />good thing it isn't. black house is spooky!. the atmosphere in this thing is just so creepy. if i never go to french landing, i will live a happy man haha. i loved the exploration of this town's people, they were all so memorable and clearly defined. and the community's response to the fisherman's murders was fascinating and infuriating to follow<br /><br />probably the most enjoyable parts of this book were the detective work in the fisherman case. it was scary and interesting. a very well written mystery. although sometimes slow, i look back on the build-up fondly. in the second half, the book shifts to a more fantastical setting with strong horror mixed in; there's a few fairly gory scenes in the action of this story. as a huge dark tower fan, i loved all the nods to the series. it's probably the book outside of the series itself containing the strongest dark tower influence. i can't imagine somebody not familiar with that series enjoying the conclusion to this book. <br /><br />anyway, i'm glad i read black house. it was a work-out but i got there in the end. it's only real flaws are that some scenes run a little long and the ending is a bit lame for the 700 paged lead-up. not wholly unsatisfying, i just maybe wanted a little more from it idk. i hope all the best for jack and now on to the final dark tower book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7773780295556259473" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2795870960" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17982115724436904789">Like Jack Sawyers, I had forgotten much about the events of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/59219.The_Talisman__The_Talisman___1_' title='The Talisman (The Talisman, #1) by Stephen King' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Talisman</a>. But as Jack recalled those events, I did as well. Often, an author will give a small recap of the previous books in a series. This didn't feel like a recap and I'm not sure it was intended to be, but it was a great way to refresh one's memory.<br/><br/>I liked that there were a lot of references to The Dark Tower series. However, the references may have had me scratching my head if I hadn't read that series. Gunslinger, Blain the Tr</span>
  <span id="freeText17982115724436904789" style="display:none">Like Jack Sawyers, I had forgotten much about the events of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/59219.The_Talisman__The_Talisman___1_" title="The Talisman (The Talisman, #1) by Stephen King" rel="nofollow noopener">The Talisman</a>. But as Jack recalled those events, I did as well. Often, an author will give a small recap of the previous books in a series. This didn't feel like a recap and I'm not sure it was intended to be, but it was a great way to refresh one's memory.<br /><br />I liked that there were a lot of references to The Dark Tower series. However, the references may have had me scratching my head if I hadn't read that series. Gunslinger, Blain the Train, the tower, the beam. Little easter eggs peppered throughout. <br /><br /></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('BYmtXQXq2BwEKO8l/ojZux68EarlKbbgjRY9UslwneZInlM744Fk1jQoxAfEEYU7IS59loig0NeVjoljkdYY2g==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('oYW8EDq3OMZqJ1oTZB9BIDuXlLLLeRE9RGjLR6kvZovskkJ23NyEDFoncTFehh2gBAX4jqbwdwpc8H928Ynjtw==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/3389.Stephen_King">About Stephen King</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/3389.Stephen_King"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1362814142p3/3389.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/3389.Stephen_King">Stephen King
</a></div>
<div class='goodreadsAuthorBadge'></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
750,366
followers

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer12966770460187596866">Stephen Edwin King was born the second son of Donald and Nellie Ruth Pillsbury King. After his father left them when Stephen was two, he and his older brother, David, were raised by his mother. Parts of his childhood were spent in Fort Wayne, Indiana, where his father's family was at the time, and in Stratford, Connecticut. When Stephen was eleven, his mother brought her children back to Durham, M</span>
  <span id="freeText12966770460187596866" style="display:none">Stephen Edwin King was born the second son of Donald and Nellie Ruth Pillsbury King. After his father left them when Stephen was two, he and his older brother, David, were raised by his mother. Parts of his childhood were spent in Fort Wayne, Indiana, where his father's family was at the time, and in Stratford, Connecticut. When Stephen was eleven, his mother brought her children back to Durham, Maine, for good. Her parents, Guy and Nellie Pillsbury, had become incapacitated with old age, and Ruth King was persuaded by her sisters to take over the physical care of them. Other family members provided a small house in Durham and financial support. After Stephen's grandparents passed away, Mrs. King found work in the kitchens of Pineland, a nearby residential facility for the mentally challenged.<br /><br />Stephen attended the grammar school in Durham and Lisbon Falls High School, graduating in 1966. From his sophomore year at the University of Maine at Orono, he wrote a weekly column for the school newspaper, THE MAINE CAMPUS. He was also active in student politics, serving as a member of the Student Senate. He came to support the anti-war movement on the Orono campus, arriving at his stance from a conservative view that the war in Vietnam was unconstitutional. He graduated in 1970, with a B.A. in English and qualified to teach on the high school level. A draft board examination immediately post-graduation found him 4-F on grounds of high blood pressure, limited vision, flat feet, and punctured eardrums.<br /><br />He met Tabitha Spruce in the stacks of the Fogler Library at the University, where they both worked as students; they married in January of 1971. As Stephen was unable to find placement as a teacher immediately, the Kings lived on his earnings as a laborer at an industrial laundry, and her student loan and savings, with an occasional boost from a short story sale to men's magazines.<br /><br />Stephen made his first professional short story sale ("The Glass Floor") to <i>Startling Mystery Stories</i> in 1967. Throughout the early years of his marriage, he continued to sell stories to men's magazines. Many were gathered into the <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10628.Night_Shift" title="Night Shift" rel="nofollow noopener">Night Shift</a> collection or appeared in other anthologies.<br /><br />In the fall of 1971, Stephen began teaching English at Hampden Academy, the public high school in Hampden, Maine. Writing in the evenings and on the weekends, he continued to produce short stories and to work on novels.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12966770460187596866" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
